This is what we received from Windstream this morning regarding the outage:

"Worklog Update: Hello, if you are receiving this message, your Windstream trouble ticket was associated to a known network event. At this time, the issue has been resolved and your services should be restored. A future planned core link had an inconsistant ISIS metric that temporarily rerouted many PE BGP sessions causing VPN route reflectors to bounce, inet-bgp session to drop and large amounts of packet loss. The configuration was corrected and the outage was resolved. If there are any further issues please contact Windstream Enterprise Repair at xxx-xxx-xxxx and reference your ticket number. Thank you."

If I had to guess, they somehow lost the more specific iBGP route to the
internal router serving that subnet and are advertising a less specific
out to the Internet. Hence the trace dies at the first hop to Verizon
regardless of entry point.

Is anybody else having issues with the Google DNS public servers?  From the Amsterdam region (specifically using the Amsterdam Internet Exchange or other peering platforms) Google DNS is unresponsive. Several other providers here see the same results.

Perhaps those who are seeing trouble with Google DNS are somehow running into this, or it was a different, transient issue that has since been resolved? Or I am simply getting a direct peering to '8.8.8.8' from the locations I am testing from, bypassing the trouble area altogether.

From jdc at koitsu.org  Thu Feb 19 18:07:04 2015

Message-ID: <20150219230704.GA8079@icarus.home.lan>

Something weird is going on with Comcast in Los Angeles: small packets
appear to be getting discarded with a loss rate of ~6-10% while larger
packets (I've tried 1000 and 1200) seem to make it through without any
loss.  Things like SSH and IMAP+SSL are impacted consistently
(particularly during key exchange), while HTTP does not appear to be, so
the issue appears to be affecting both TCP and ICMP (have not tested
UDP).

First sign of this issue, according to my logs, is at 11:51 PT (UTC-8),
and has gradually gotten worse over the past few hours.

Looks like the issue is with the forward path (Source->Destination
listed below), as the return path only shows loss at the final
destination.  (I currently cannot provide a return-path mtr because the
only way I can access my box is through VNC, and I don't like doing
things like screenshots of a VNC window, so you'll just have to trust
me)

Nothing anomalous shows up when using L3's looking glass to ping things,
and the only Comcast LG I know of is in NYC.

I most likely won't see Email responses from anyone (directly or to the
list) until this problem is addressed, since my mail is hosted on shown
box and cannot currently be fetched due to the problem.  Frustrating.

Source IP: 69.181.142.213
Destination IP: 174.136.108.146

> listed below), as the return path only shows loss at the final

> me)

From lists at tigertech.com  Thu Feb 19 18:32:09 2015
From: lists at tigertech.com (Robert L Mathews)
Date: Thu, 19 Feb 2015 15:32:09 -0800
Subject: [outages] Comcast LA issue?
In-Reply-To: <20150219230704.GA8079@icarus.home.lan>
References: <20150219230704.GA8079@icarus.home.lan>
Message-ID: <54E67279.6070407@tigertech.com>

On 2/19/15 3:07 PM, Jeremy Chadwick via Outages wrote:
> Something weird is going on with Comcast in Los Angeles: small packets
> appear to be getting discarded with a loss rate of ~6-10% while larger
> packets (I've tried 1000 and 1200) seem to make it through without any
> loss.  Things like SSH and IMAP+SSL are impacted consistently
> (particularly during key exchange), while HTTP does not appear to be, so
> the issue appears to be affecting both TCP and ICMP (have not tested
> UDP).

Seeing similar things in the San Francisco Bay Area for the last few hours.

Certain combinations of IP addresses/ports/protocols/packet sizes
completely fail or have > 30% packet loss; changing one of those
variables changes the result.

This results in neat things like "HTTP from a browser fails, but 'telnet
host 80', 'GET / HTTP/1.0' works just fine".

Lots of probably similar problems here:

 https://downdetector.com/status/comcast-xfinity/san-francisco

-- 
Robert L Mathews, Tiger Technologies, http://www.tigertech.net/

on the return path).  Look about right?

> > On Thu, Feb 19, 2015 at 03:07:04PM -0800, Jeremy Chadwick wrote:
> > > Something weird is going on with Comcast in Los Angeles: small packets
> > > appear to be getting discarded with a loss rate of ~6-10% while larger
> > > packets (I've tried 1000 and 1200) seem to make it through without any
> > > loss.  Things like SSH and IMAP+SSL are impacted consistently
> > > (particularly during key exchange), while HTTP does not appear to be, so
> > > the issue appears to be affecting both TCP and ICMP (have not tested
> > > UDP).
> > >
> > > First sign of this issue, according to my logs, is at 11:51 PT (UTC-8),
> > > and has gradually gotten worse over the past few hours.
> > >
> > > Looks like the issue is with the forward path (Source->Destination
> > > listed below), as the return path only shows loss at the final
> > > destination.  (I currently cannot provide a return-path mtr because the
> > > only way I can access my box is through VNC, and I don't like doing
> > > things like screenshots of a VNC window, so you'll just have to trust
> > > me)
> > >
> > > Nothing anomalous shows up when using L3's looking glass to ping things,

From billw at waveform.net  Thu Feb 26 13:27:52 2015
From: billw at waveform.net (Bill Wichers)
Date: Thu, 26 Feb 2015 18:27:52 +0000
Subject: [outages] FW: Vandalism of CenturyLink fibre in Arizona causes large outage footprint.
References: <DF79D428-67AA-4853-9762-472FE071EE01@arbor.net>
 <CANB6qCgpuj-RbB+-khPHah8S6-V6+a5o0ptgQv6BO98EG6YdcQ@mail.gmail.com> 
Message-ID: <4897906C085783429A2F4B39EBFF44F078BADE32@Server-01.WaveformTechnology.local>

It?s possible that there were multiple, marginal issues. An OTDR will find a break or major discontinuity (severe bend, etc.) An OTDR will *not* show minor faults like abraded sheats, rodent damage that hasn?t reached the fibers yet, etc. If the techs found vandalism in some areas that didn?t break strands, they would have been suspicious and started looking more closely along the line to find out what else *might* be going on. Essentially preventative maintenance.

I?m just saying that it might not be all PR spin?

  -Bill

>> in the 2013 san jose cut, the cable was severed in two places, making
>> the distance to break different from both ends.
>
>
> not running an OTDR from both ends to determine the extent of the break and
> any damage to the cable (such as stretching) is incompetence... I'd hope the
> long distance field engineers understood how to analyse and repair a break


It's entirely *possible* that the CL engineers are completely
incompetent and presently peering into the EDFAs while repeatedly
pushing the Laser Shutdown Override and saying to each other "I think
I saw it flash, do that again..."

I suspect that it is *much* more likely that whoever the press called
is entirely non-technical, but trying to be helpful and explaining
what *they* know at the moment.
The story that ends up in the paper is often wildly different from
what an engineer would say..

> (then again, I'd hope they knew how to build a redundant network too)

Nod.
